  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ae3250a8-fdc7-482a-93a4-f514783f8496'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15159885718104828773">Four childhood friends in present-day New Orleans are torn apart by envy, passion, and a secret murder.<br/><br/>Five years ago, Meredith, Brandon, Greg, and Stephen quickly discover the fragile boundaries between friendship and betrayal as they enter high school and form new allegiances. Meredith, Brandon, and Greg gain popularity, while Stephen is viciously treated as an outcast. </span>
  <span id="freeText15159885718104828773" style="display:none">Four childhood friends in present-day New Orleans are torn apart by envy, passion, and a secret murder.<br /><br />Five years ago, Meredith, Brandon, Greg, and Stephen quickly discover the fragile boundaries between friendship and betrayal as they enter high school and form new allegiances. Meredith, Brandon, and Greg gain popularity, while Stephen is viciously treated as an outcast. Then two violent deaths destroy the already delicate bonds of their friendship.<br /><br />When the friends are drawn back together, new facts about their mutual history are exposed and what was held to be a tragic accident is revealed as murder. As the true story emerges, other secrets begin to unravel with more dangerous, far-reaching consequences.<br /><br /><i>A Density of Souls</i> is a stunning debut novel that uncovers the darker side of the teenage psyche.</span>

<div id="review_199054109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199054109" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6052564-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1313590665p2/6052564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199054109?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/6052564-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199054109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer131913624957199671">The gay and lesbian fiction genre is awash with tragically short sighted, stereotypical, and hard to get through novels about coming out, getting beat up, and either finding love or ending up dead. Christopher Rice is like a lighthouse on the banks of a bleak and dismal ocean of the GLBTQ genre. Rice's works are more about a good story, where the character(s) happen to be gay- not a novel solely revolving around the fact that one of the characters like sex with the same gender. <br/><br/>Destiny of Souls </span>
  <span id="freeText131913624957199671" style="display:none">The gay and lesbian fiction genre is awash with tragically short sighted, stereotypical, and hard to get through novels about coming out, getting beat up, and either finding love or ending up dead. Christopher Rice is like a lighthouse on the banks of a bleak and dismal ocean of the GLBTQ genre. Rice's works are more about a good story, where the character(s) happen to be gay- not a novel solely revolving around the fact that one of the characters like sex with the same gender. <br /><br />Destiny of Souls is Rice's (yes, he is Anne Rice's son) first novel and it happens to be my favorite. Rice's depiction of modern day New Orleans, and the complicated web of a group of high school friends is poignant and beautiful. If you are familiar with the GLBTQ fiction genre and you find yourself sick of the trash like "Boston Boys Club" and "Bound By Law" then pick up a book by Rice and just see if it fits for you like it did for me- hopefully you'll love it enough to join Rice for his other works (my next personal favorite is Moonlit Earth- which is about a gay flight attendant who is wrongly accused of being a terrorist and his sister takes it upon herself to clear his name. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="131913624957199671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570029415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5184992006742676151">I won't be writing a full, detailed review for Christopher Rice's <b>
  <i>A Density of Souls</i>
</b>, but I will say that it was an important, spectacular read. It's a must have for anyone who's ever been victimized or bullied, and definitely anyone who considers themselves part of the LGBTQ+ community. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lukas Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lukas Anthony" href="/user/show/10117401-lukas-anthony">Lukas Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421284208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15861881365474421599"><b>Christopher Rice loves melodrama.</b><br/><br/>I had no idea before starting this that Christopher Rice is the son of Vampire author Anne Rice (whose works I've never properly ready anyway) but it was interesting to see that he had followed in his mother's footsteps, minus vampire's of course. <br/><br/>What I can say about this novel is that it's 'okay'. The writing is quite good, and a picture of the town and situation is handled nicely but I felt everything got very melodramatic very quickly. This is a novel that in</span>
  <span id="freeText15861881365474421599" style="display:none"><b>Christopher Rice loves melodrama.</b><br /><br />I had no idea before starting this that Christopher Rice is the son of Vampire author Anne Rice (whose works I've never properly ready anyway) but it was interesting to see that he had followed in his mother's footsteps, minus vampire's of course. <br /><br />What I can say about this novel is that it's 'okay'. The writing is quite good, and a picture of the town and situation is handled nicely but I felt everything got very melodramatic very quickly. This is a novel that includes mass murder, suicides (by the plenty), rape, domestic abuse, a husband who has drugged his wife into a coma for five years, infidelity, self-harm, alcoholism....it get's to be a lot of issues very quickly. Then come the end of the novel, in case none of that was enough, the author has a hurricane hit the town, for well, no real reason other than because he can. It got a bit much.<br /><br />Character wise nobody really stood out, it never felt like there was a main character...sometimes it even felt like there were too many. I found myself routinely getting confused as to who was related to who. They were not distinctive enough either, basically all I felt from them is that they were all depressed in some way. <br /><br />Overall an easy book to finish but not one that I would recommend. The same story has been told much better before, and I found it to be quite an empty read, which isn't really what you want when dealing with the topics and issues that this book does. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15861881365474421599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189743716?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.Z. Snow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.Z. Snow" href="/user/show/2135051-k-z-snow">K.Z. Snow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786866465" href="/book/show/684589.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189743716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9940550940140566985"><b>3.5</b><br/><br/>The novels of Chris Rice might just become one of my guilty pleasures. In spite of <i>and</i> because of its abundant flaws, this was a whopping good, Flannery-O'Connor-meets-Jacqueline-Susann read.<br/><br/>Daytime soaps can't hold a candle to this book. Oy, the excess! Multiple murders and mayhem; suicide and insanity; alcoholism and bulimia; rape, infidelity, incest; bullying, spousal abuse, and effed-up families; homosexuality and homophobia (and rivers of tears); New Orleans cemeteries; jocks and cheerle</span>
  <span id="freeText9940550940140566985" style="display:none"><b>3.5</b><br /><br />The novels of Chris Rice might just become one of my guilty pleasures. In spite of <i>and</i> because of its abundant flaws, this was a whopping good, Flannery-O'Connor-meets-Jacqueline-Susann read.<br /><br />Daytime soaps can't hold a candle to this book. Oy, the excess! Multiple murders and mayhem; suicide and insanity; alcoholism and bulimia; rape, infidelity, incest; bullying, spousal abuse, and effed-up families; homosexuality and homophobia (and rivers of tears); New Orleans cemeteries; jocks and cheerleaders, gay boyz in musicals, and a cute kid hit by a truck. A terrorist group with terrorist plots! Explosions! A major hurricane complete with submariner rats!<br /> <br /><i>Phrew</i>. There is danger and dysfunction at every turn of the page. It's a breathtaking, brow-wiping ride.<br /><br />Precious few of the characters are well developed or sympathetic. And there are a lot of them. And the POV ebulliently hippity-hops among them all. (Every player in this melodrama has, it seems, a point of view.) It's sort of like omniscient combined with <i>ah, WTF, let's drop in on <u>this</u> person's thoughts for a few lines</i>.<br /><br />But . . . the story kept me engaged. I didn't even mind the proofreader's oversights too much. And I was mostly pleased with the ending (just would've liked to see Mary Sue Meredith bite the mud). </span>
  <a data-text-id="9940550940140566985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1123417373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7434391827330436557">REVIEW A DENSITY OF SOULS by Christopher Rice<br/><br/>I had read much comment on this book at first publication in 2002, but not the book. Once I read THE HEAVENS RISE, I realized Mr. Rice should be one of my always-read authors, and reading his most recent novel, THE VINES, only confirmed that. So I am gratified that his earlier novels are being republished, and decided to start with A DENSITY OF SOULS, his first.<br/><br/>I found this not gory at all, but saddening. For some reason, even after more than six deca</span>
  <span id="freeText7434391827330436557" style="display:none">REVIEW A DENSITY OF SOULS by Christopher Rice<br /><br />I had read much comment on this book at first publication in 2002, but not the book. Once I read THE HEAVENS RISE, I realized Mr. Rice should be one of my always-read authors, and reading his most recent novel, THE VINES, only confirmed that. So I am gratified that his earlier novels are being republished, and decided to start with A DENSITY OF SOULS, his first.<br /><br />I found this not gory at all, but saddening. For some reason, even after more than six decades of living, reading both fiction and nonfiction, historical and contemporary, I find myself still unaccountably startled and shocked whenever evidence of the depravity of the human soul rears its ugly self. I'm speaking here of bigotry, domestic violence, the compulsion to control, and of course homophobia. I felt such empathy for Stephen, and some for his mother Monica. I can't say as much for Meredith (whom I wanted to like but could not), Greg, or Brandon. I do.know this: after I finished the book last night, I didn't want to read anything else right away. A DENSITY OF SOULS lingered all night in my mind, and continues to claim a place there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7434391827330436557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone, young adult and older.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116373832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10445201048357717060">I've read this book twice now, which is something I rarely do. It is a must read and still my favorite work of his. Although I have yet to read his newest that I picked up earlier this year at a book signing in San Diego. I'm actually reading through his previous works to savor his new release. 1st read: Dec 2000<br/><br/>I feel that I should really add more to this. This book has a main character who is gay, but in no means does it come of preachy in concern with that. This book is about the struggles be</span>
  <span id="freeText10445201048357717060" style="display:none">I've read this book twice now, which is something I rarely do. It is a must read and still my favorite work of his. Although I have yet to read his newest that I picked up earlier this year at a book signing in San Diego. I'm actually reading through his previous works to savor his new release. 1st read: Dec 2000<br /><br />I feel that I should really add more to this. This book has a main character who is gay, but in no means does it come of preachy in concern with that. This book is about the struggles between people that their differences cause. It also hits on the underlying lies of a social group and how conforming comes with a price. It is beautifully done and if I remember correctly he wrote it at 22. I was a teenager when it came out and it stirred the creativity in me in a way that I didn't feel until years later when I met Christopher Rice himself at a book signing. I remembered my love of writing. After reading this a second time I started working on a book which is something I have always wanted to do, but didn't because of the fear of rejection. Between his words, written and spoken, I have decided to write for myself. I just find his work, especially this first book, to be inspiring.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15813649398200401834">Not very good at all. It reminded me of the books I read when I was ten or twelve years old: Christopher Pike and V.C. Andrews had a love child that puked up this tripe. I could barely get through the first few chapters because I kept rolling my eyes or cringing at the terrible writing.   <span id="freeText15813649398200401834" style="display:none">Not very good at all. It reminded me of the books I read when I was ten or twelve years old: Christopher Pike and V.C. Andrews had a love child that puked up this tripe. I could barely get through the first few chapters because I kept rolling my eyes or cringing at the terrible writing. Also, I understand that this is gay literature but it seems like all the men in this book are gay... and boring. All the various shocking truths that are revealed throughout I mostly figured out waaaaay before the author gets around to writing about them and the twist at the end seemed so unnecessary (but so obvious) that I doubt I will read any of the author's other books. I gave the book a second star because the book got better as it went on although it really should be a one and a half star rating. Finally, there was not one character in this book that was well developed; they all seemed like cardboard cutouts of where real characters should be. Don't bother.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9108256953341816915">WAAAAYYY TOO MUCH GOING ON! The reason for the two star rating is that the premise of the story is a really good one: 4 childhood friends are torn apart in their young adult lives by cruelty, lies, secrets and murder veiled as an unfortunate tradgedy.<br/><br/>A Density of Souls, unfortunately did not stop there.   <span id="freeText9108256953341816915" style="display:none">WAAAAYYY TOO MUCH GOING ON! The reason for the two star rating is that the premise of the story is a really good one: 4 childhood friends are torn apart in their young adult lives by cruelty, lies, secrets and murder veiled as an unfortunate tradgedy.<br /><br />A Density of Souls, unfortunately did not stop there. There were more than a dozen confusing points of view, at least half as many tragic, over the top scenarios, and more melodrama than a body can stand.<br /><br />Seriously, homosexuality/homophobia, bullying, alcoholism, physical abuse, Bullemia, rape, murder, drug abuse, incest and a friggen natural disaster! Too. Much.<br /><br />The editing was non existant as you jumped from memory to current day, from one narrative to another, all in a blink with no time to digest a new revelation or catch your breath from a horrific moment. <br /><br />With so much going on and so many characters offering their viewpoints, what you end up with is a ridiculously jumbled and disjointed collections of shorts that were forced together in an attempt to create a story. It just doesn't work.<br /><br />There is a promise of a thrilling, engrossing story here, if only Christopher were willing to cut out all but the necessary charcters and keep the main plot points to two instead of a dozen.<br /><br />Anyhoo, that's my opinion.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3392037108224681272">Wow. I just finished this book and I don't even know really where to begin. The beginning years in high school resonated heavily with me and drew me into the story ASAP. The story and Rice's writing kept me enthralled. Everyone here is flawed, troubled, and broken. It seemed as though nothing yet also everything was happening as y</span>
  <span id="freeText3392037108224681272" style="display:none">Wow. I just finished this book and I don't even know really where to begin. The beginning years in high school resonated heavily with me and drew me into the story ASAP. The story and Rice's writing kept me enthralled. Everyone here is flawed, troubled, and broken. The novel is so tragically written that you cannot wallowing in the events that take place throughout the book. I felt this was a super slow-burn but not in a bad way. It seemed as though nothing yet also everything was happening as you read. With little action to carry the reader through the story, Rice shines in his characterizations and story-telling that keep you invested. There is a light mystery or two at the core of everything that comes to a head at the end, but you'll go through 250ish pages before things really pick up pace; but I didn't care in the least. I'm still left in awe of what I have read and comprehending it all as it sinks. I'm eager to read other works by Rice as I have heard so many great things! </span>

<div id="review_741012804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/741012804" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741012804?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anton" href="/user/show/5876597-anton">Anton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741012804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17071404578977303429">***SPOILERSPOILERSPOILER***<br/><br/>OK so by the time this 270 page slim (but still interminable) novel ends, the author has thrown in all of the following:<br/><br/>Murder<br/>Rape<br/>Child death<br/>Incest<br/>A nightclub bombing<br/>A gay man who has the magical ability to turn straight men gay<br/>Insanity<br/>Cults<br/>Alcoholism<br/>Forced drugging<br/>And to top it all off A HURRICANE as its climax!<br/><br/>Yet despite Rice heaving practically every exhausting calamity he could think of against his uninteresting characters (except for cannibalism which I half expe</span>
  <span id="freeText17071404578977303429" style="display:none">***SPOILERSPOILERSPOILER***<br /><br />OK so by the time this 270 page slim (but still interminable) novel ends, the author has thrown in all of the following:<br /><br />Murder<br />Rape<br />Child death<br />Incest<br />A nightclub bombing<br />A gay man who has the magical ability to turn straight men gay<br />Insanity<br />Cults<br />Alcoholism<br />Forced drugging<br />And to top it all off A HURRICANE as its climax!<br /><br />Yet despite Rice heaving practically every exhausting calamity he could think of against his uninteresting characters (except for cannibalism which I half expected to turn up at some point), none of the turns the story took were surprising or shocking. Perhaps because early on this book took on the tone of a really bad American soap for me. It felt like a year in the world of Days Of Our Lives.<br /><br />This book has a fairly good rating on Goodreads. My theories are as follows: <br /><br />1. He was 22 when he wrote this, his debut. Cut him some slack. I'll admit, when I was 22 I was prone to hyperbole. Still, I'm offering no slack.<br /><br />2. He is the son of Anne Rice a famous novelist who is someone I will probably never read. Perhaps his having a famous mum has bestowed critical favours on him.<br /><br />3. This book is reasonably heavily gay themed and perhaps many in the gay community have been a little lenient on Rice for this novel. They shouldn't be. Please read some James Baldwin and Alan Hollinghurst.<br /><br />This was just far too much to bear. With all of the eventfulness of the novel it could have been a campy pleasure. But it took itself way too seriously and failed to achieve anything. <br /><br />Further recommendations for excellent gay literature however are very welcome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17071404578977303429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196408420" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196408420" />
    <a title="Kitty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4032367-kitty"><img alt="Kitty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419977972p2/4032367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196408420?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kitty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kitty" href="/user/show/4032367-kitty">Kitty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786866465" href="/book/show/684589.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196408420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14534826232821469637">Alright, so Christopher Rice isn't exactly the most polished of writers. There were parts in this that ranged from melodramatic to downright farcical - the big show down in the eye of the hurricane was so completely over the top that I read the whole thing in my mind using Ru Paul's voice. And you know what? I still think this is a pretty good book. In an ever growing sea of at best, second rate gay fiction that floods the market between covers featuring sweaty, muscle ripped hunkies, Souls is a</span>
  <span id="freeText14534826232821469637" style="display:none">Alright, so Christopher Rice isn't exactly the most polished of writers. There were parts in this that ranged from melodramatic to downright farcical - the big show down in the eye of the hurricane was so completely over the top that I read the whole thing in my mind using Ru Paul's voice. And you know what? I still think this is a pretty good book. In an ever growing sea of at best, second rate gay fiction that floods the market between covers featuring sweaty, muscle ripped hunkies, Souls is a surprisingly tender debut.<br /><br />What ends up ultimately redeeming A Density of Souls are two things. One is the fact that Rice has the innate ability to accurately capture the smallest details of misery and survival facing teens. Sure the big stuff might be questionable, but Stephen's conversation to his drama teacher in which he asks "when does it end?" hits right at the heart. Anyone who ever suffered from an extended period of bullying knows just what he means when he says he would welcome the isolation that becoming a high school pariah would afford him if only it would remove him from his tormentor's attention. Rice is never afraid to infuse his characters with a lot of emotion.<br /><br />The second is that Rice maintains a very firm grounding in the world he writes about. There may be more talented writers out there, but if they can't convince themselves about the world they're writing about how can they expect to fool us, willing victims, for even a little while. What Rice lacks in the firmness of his prose, he more than makes up for with the clarity of his vision as he lovingly describes French Quarter bars, back seat dates, drunken parties, mental health facilities and lonely beaches. Perhaps the reason I came to care to much for these characters is because in Rice's hands they become real people. And maybe in that sense the roughness to the writing works for, rather than against, the story. After all when in real life do we ever meet people who emerge into our lives fully written, polished to perfection and willing to let us see the faults written in our own characters by knowing the absence in theirs?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14534826232821469637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="So, I Read This Book Today" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8823926-so-i-read-this-book-today"><img alt="So, I Read This Book Today" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385785384p2/8823926.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1164160422?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="So, I Read This Book Today" class="user" itemprop="url" name="So, I Read This Book Today" href="/user/show/8823926-so-i-read-this-book-today">So, I Read This Book Today</a>
      </span>

  <span id="freeText3018258212031494751" style="display:none">From the deepest desires often come the deadliest hate. - Socrates<br /><br />Expectations. I think that is always my problem when I read “name” authors. With their fancy publishers, fancy marketing and ‘names’ I expect their work to be bigger, more well written, deeper. And, honestly, after The Vines I had expected more just because that book was better. It had deeper structure, a better story line. <br /><br />I understand Christopher’s thought processes, and I honor them. This time, however, I feel he is trying too hard, pushing instead of leading if that makes sense. Don’t get me wrong. There are good things about the book, things that are important. But the overall issues meant the book simply didn’t work for me. I look forward to seeing what others find to love about it.<br /><br />I received this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. All thoughts are my own. Should you appreciate my reviews please don’t hesitate to click “Yes” for “Was this review helpful to you?” Thanks!<br /></span>

<div id="review_2884349278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2884349278" />
    <a title="E. Denise Billups" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46114314-e-denise-billups"><img alt="E. Denise Billups" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505854188p2/46114314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2884349278?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E. Denise Billups" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E. Denise Billups" href="/user/show/46114314-e-denise-billups">E. Denise Billups</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2884349278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13970282604487911475">This is my second book by Christopher Rice, and I enjoyed his psychological thriller/coming-of-age story set in contemporary New Orleans. The mood is ominous, brooding with tightly wound emotions. Homoerotic desires and secrets unravel in unspeakable violence amidst four childhood friends. Seams unravel bit by bit as murder and suicide undo four friendships, climaxing with a hurricane that washes away madness brought on by years of jealousy, passion, hatred, tainting not only the main character’</span>
  <span id="freeText13970282604487911475" style="display:none">This is my second book by Christopher Rice, and I enjoyed his psychological thriller/coming-of-age story set in contemporary New Orleans. The mood is ominous, brooding with tightly wound emotions. Homoerotic desires and secrets unravel in unspeakable violence amidst four childhood friends. Seams unravel bit by bit as murder and suicide undo four friendships, climaxing with a hurricane that washes away madness brought on by years of jealousy, passion, hatred, tainting not only the main character’s friendship, but also their families, and the entire town.<br /><br />The story centers around four main Meredith Ducite, Stephen Conlin, Brandon Charbonnet, and Greg Darby. The story begins the Summer of 1992 as the four ride their bikes through Lafayette cemetery to play a game of hide-and-seek while a storm brews overhead. It is here that Meredith witnesses incomprehensible act between Greg and Stephen. She wants to believe it’s just boys play, but on a deeper level, she knows it’s something else. <br /><br /> “Greg and Stephen locked eyes with an intensity that told Meredith they were part of a world <br /> she had been denied access to. It had to be a world known only to boys.”<br /><br />Soon after the four enter Cannon, a private school for privileged teens, the friendship splinters. Cannon halls are filled with adolescent behaviors and cruelties toward other’s differences. After rumors of Stephens sexual inclination, he’s bullied and ostracized freshman year. <br /><br /> “During his first morning at Cannon Stephen’s only companion was the collective din of <br /> whispers, snickers, and openly disdainful glares.”<br /><br />Meredith soon spirals into bulimia and alcoholism. Brandon and Greg become popular football stars, hiding their fears and doubts behind masculinity, and bullying Stephen with homophobic slurs and violent acts. But beneath the anger and hatred lies lust, jealousies, and madness, leading to murder, suicide, and unstable adulthoods tainted by adolescent scars. <br /><br />The story climaxes with an unveiled family secret, threatening an already fragile bond between the main characters. A hurricane sweeps in as if to wipe the slate clean―purge the past and pull a secret into the light. Furious flood waters bring atonement and a fresh start for Meredith and Stephen. This story has many twists and turns steamier than Louisiana’s summer ―tension, lusts, anger, madness… Phew! <br /><br />The author delved deeply into teenage cruelty, fear, and persecution. I thoroughly enjoyed Mr. Rice’s well-written, turbulent coming-of-age story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13970282604487911475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2122356399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122356399" />
    <a title="Adam Cook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57705525-adam-cook"><img alt="Adam Cook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468890765p2/57705525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2122356399?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Cook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Cook" href="/user/show/57705525-adam-cook">Adam Cook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2122356399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4321072586459362556">I've read a fair amount of books. Hundreds rather than thousands, I'll admit, but you could say i read at a decent clip. Many of these books are bad. I've read books with bad writing but good stories. I've read books with great writing but poor stories. But i don't think I've read a book that is quite so lacking in merit as this one ever. The writing is decent, yes. It's fine. And it was nice to see some LGBT representation in a novel also (although it was definitely just the G and no LBT that i</span>
  <span id="freeText4321072586459362556" style="display:none">I've read a fair amount of books. Hundreds rather than thousands, I'll admit, but you could say i read at a decent clip. Many of these books are bad. I've read books with bad writing but good stories. I've read books with great writing but poor stories. But i don't think I've read a book that is quite so lacking in merit as this one ever. The writing is decent, yes. It's fine. And it was nice to see some LGBT representation in a novel also (although it was definitely just the G and no LBT that i remember). But every single other aspect of this novel is catastrophic. I'd rather read a bad novel than a boring one but this novel is both. Yet i still finished it...<br /><br />The truth is that i couldn't put it down. I needed to know how it could possibly get worse. I DID want to know what happened in the end but absolutely not for the right reasons. <br /><br />I don't think I've read elsewhere a novel which is so confused. Descriptions of locations mean nothing. Character actions, thoughts and feelings sometimes contradict and sometimes even make zero sense. Characters shout at each other and strike out for no discernible reason. It's BONKERS. <br /><br />And not in a good way. Twin Peaks was weird and had odd characters being odd...but that was intentional. This is just macabre in how bad it is. <br /><br />I didn't like anyone in the book. I didn't care for anyone. These people existed briefly in my mind and will very soon return to nothing. And not a moment too soon.<br /><br />In a word: wretched.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4321072586459362556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2013502552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5446907-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510539844p2/5446907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013502552?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/5446907-alicia">Alicia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013502552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10650723246420499390">He ain't lyin' with that title, ya'll. This book is DENSE with souls - literally.<br/><br/>That said, this was a great read. I quickly sorted out who was who and became emotionally invested. This is Christopher Rice's first novel but I liked it a lot more than Vines, which is the only other piece of his I've read. <br/><br/>I know he wasn't aiming for a "coming of age story set in New Orleans" but that's what this is... that the characters coming of age are a popular cheerleader, a bullied gay teen, and a complete </span>
  <span id="freeText10650723246420499390" style="display:none">He ain't lyin' with that title, ya'll. This book is DENSE with souls - literally.<br /><br />That said, this was a great read. I quickly sorted out who was who and became emotionally invested. This is Christopher Rice's first novel but I liked it a lot more than Vines, which is the only other piece of his I've read. <br /><br />I know he wasn't aiming for a "coming of age story set in New Orleans" but that's what this is... that the characters coming of age are a popular cheerleader, a bullied gay teen, and a complete fuckwad of a villain is without question. <br /><br />Definitely a great read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10650723246420499390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_691667525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691667525" />
    <a title="Jonathan de Lange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22837098-jonathan-de-lange"><img alt="Jonathan de Lange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375712688p2/22837098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/691667525?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan de Lange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan de Lange" href="/user/show/22837098-jonathan-de-lange">Jonathan de Lange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691667525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17068606861116343707">From the first word to the final punctuation, this book intrigued me. It legitimately enticed me to keep reading. Not a single character was dull and while their motivations were often a mystery to the me as I read (as I believe they were supposed to be) they were never boring and were always worth my time.<br/><br/>I can spend much time going on about this book and how it struck a chord with me, but let's focus on the simple fact that it gave me something to chew on. It is often the case that books prete</span>
  <span id="freeText17068606861116343707" style="display:none">From the first word to the final punctuation, this book intrigued me. It legitimately enticed me to keep reading. Not a single character was dull and while their motivations were often a mystery to the me as I read (as I believe they were supposed to be) they were never boring and were always worth my time.<br /><br />I can spend much time going on about this book and how it struck a chord with me, but let's focus on the simple fact that it gave me something to chew on. It is often the case that books pretend to be profound when in truth, they are easy teasers that are quite easily willing to give you their secrets after a few minutes of tussling with them.<br /><br />Not this book.<br /><br />Christopher Rice manages to always give you just the right amount of who-did-what-to-who to leave you with new and unanswered questions each time, therefore propelling you further into a story that battles with the loss of innocence, the confusion of youth and the fear of the unknown. <br /><br />The erratic movement between POV is actually refreshing as far as I'm concerned and each character contributes, in however small a manner, to a greater scheme. From the main character Stephen, who acts as the world's punching bag most of the time, to Trish Ducote, notable more for her substantial absence from both the book and her daughters life, each character had a reason. It was heartening to me, actually, that there were few peripheral characters and that only those who were necessary for the story were used for extended periods. <br /><br />Does the story have a point? <br /><br />Definitely. The only problem is, it offers us no solution to the problems it presents us with. It offers no answers to any moral dilemma the reader is presented with.<br /><br />Is it a bad thing?<br /><br />Not at all. As with our own lives, the characters find no solutions to their own problems, thus leaving them unable to give us any solutions. The characters face the problems, but stumble over them as stunted youths (which they mostly are) rather than process them and deal with them since they've never learned how to do that (the adult characters don't do a great job of passing on any pearls of wisdom.)<br /><br />The story does, however, leave us with the one thing the characters do have though. Hope. <br /><br />Cheese and cliche... but still the truth. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17068606861116343707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_431741448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/431741448" />
    <a title="Tricia Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2472893-tricia-sutton"><img alt="Tricia Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246926522p2/2472893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/431741448?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tricia Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tricia Sutton" href="/user/show/2472893-tricia-sutton">Tricia Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431741448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8021316901573848812">I wish books these days had a synopsis on the back jacket like in the old days. Because I literally bought this book for its cover. The dark foreboding cover, the graveyard statue, and the title all suggested a spooky book, perfect for Halloween month. Additionally the book is also missing an author page. I had no idea what was getting into. Had I known the author was the son of Anne Rice, it would have further tempted me to thinking spook fest.<br/><br/>Nothing in the beginning gave me clues to the contr</span>
  <span id="freeText8021316901573848812" style="display:none">I wish books these days had a synopsis on the back jacket like in the old days. Because I literally bought this book for its cover. The dark foreboding cover, the graveyard statue, and the title all suggested a spooky book, perfect for Halloween month. Additionally the book is also missing an author page. I had no idea what was getting into. Had I known the author was the son of Anne Rice, it would have further tempted me to thinking spook fest.<br /><br />Nothing in the beginning gave me clues to the contrary: begins in a New Orleans graveyard, kids playing hide n seek, trapped there by a rainstorm, then one of them gets freaky with a poem, all of it ingredients for a horror story. And then ... nothing. This whole book was gay love and homophobia. If I had read that description on the book jacket I would have at first thought it was a mistake since it didn't match the cover or title, then I would have put it down simply because it's not a story for me. I can read stories with gay main characters, that is not a problem, but I don't like "issues" stories because then the character seems only about that. In fact I could not relate to any of the characters, gay or straight, they were stereotypical and cliched.<br /><br />My last gripe is for all authors who use similar names in their novels. Mr. Rice is guilty of having a Monica, Meredith, and Melissa (or was it Melanie? I don't know they were all the same after a while). The pause to recollect who is who at each name each time was an inconvenient trip up. Why why why can't they see what they are doing? So many authors do this. What? Do they have a dictionary of baby names to select character names and stay within the same letter of the alphabet? Geez people. <br /><br />Other than the above, I finished this book, and, for the most part, found it entertaining. But come on Christopher, it's like you want to write drama but felt you had to trick Anne Rice fans into thinking they are getting one of her novels. Next time strike out on your own without all the mama Rice feel to it. I felt a little deceived. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8021316901573848812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90049192?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330489331" href="/book/show/99641.A_Density_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299030-adrian?shelf=gay">gay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299030-adrian?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299030-adrian?shelf=noir">noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299030-adrian?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299030-adrian?shelf=southern-gothic">southern-gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90049192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13313937363747937010">After reading this book for the 5th or 6th time, I'm finally ready to offer a review. What Rice has done is pen a debut novel that is both compelling and entertaining. He shows a voice that has his mother's flare for the poetic and evocative while also being wholly original. In A Density of Souls, he creates a cast of characters that are each wonderfully original and unique. It's a wonderful story about love, loss, the scars of the past, and the strength and weaknesses of childhood friendships. </span>
  <span id="freeText13313937363747937010" style="display:none">After reading this book for the 5th or 6th time, I'm finally ready to offer a review. What Rice has done is pen a debut novel that is both compelling and entertaining. He shows a voice that has his mother's flare for the poetic and evocative while also being wholly original. In A Density of Souls, he creates a cast of characters that are each wonderfully original and unique. It's a wonderful story about love, loss, the scars of the past, and the strength and weaknesses of childhood friendships. This is a book that should be read by everyone. It is all show and no tell. Rice's New Orleans is a place that's equal parts beauty and deep scared history in which the secrets kept weigh heavy on the souls of those keeping them. This is the first novel by Christopher Rice, but it's written as if it were penned by a seasoned professional and it clearly marks the beginning of what has become a very auspicious career. Of everything I've ever read that isn't a Harry Potter book or wasn't written by this man's mother, this is my all time favorite. I look forward to the next time I find myself getting lost in its pages with baited breath.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10160656037405533874">I started to read the book A Density of Souls by Christopher Rice with no expectations. I had read his book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22780816.The_Vines' title='The Vines by Christopher Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vines</a> recently and I liked it, so I chose another book of his from NetGalley as well.<br/><br/>At the beginning it's all confusing, so many different story lines, so many different characters, but as the story goes on I actually started to enjoy all those small stories that combine together a really good story and at the end it was a "nail bitting and siting at edge your seat" good, it was reall</span>
  <span id="freeText10160656037405533874" style="display:none">I started to read the book A Density of Souls by Christopher Rice with no expectations. I had read his book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22780816.The_Vines" title="The Vines by Christopher Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vines</a> recently and I liked it, so I chose another book of his from NetGalley as well.<br /><br />At the beginning it's all confusing, so many different story lines, so many different characters, but as the story goes on I actually started to enjoy all those small stories that combine together a really good story and at the end it was a "nail bitting and siting at edge your seat" good, it was really hard to put it down.<br /><br />I agree with authors preface - <i>If you are looking for a gritty, realistic portrayal of high school students coming of age in New Orleans, look elsewhere; this is not that book. If you are looking for a delicate social chronicle of gay life in the New Orleans French Quarter, look elsewhere; this is not that book. If you are looking for vampires or witches, sorry, but you've got the wrong Rice.</i> The best way to read this book is with open mind and without expectations.<br /><br />For me it was really enjoyable experience.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patti" href="/user/show/1698762-patti">Patti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46338580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2761319691172688255">Oy- not sure where to begin here. I picked this book up rather randomly from some used book shelves (the price was right) and did not make the author's association with Anne Rice right away (but the dark theme is ultimately resonant). Nor did I realize that this would be classified as "gay fiction." Before I realized all that I got about twenty pages into the book and was not sure it would be one that I could finish...too many characters that were initially confusing and not capturing my interes</span>
  <span id="freeText2761319691172688255" style="display:none">Oy- not sure where to begin here. I picked this book up rather randomly from some used book shelves (the price was right) and did not make the author's association with Anne Rice right away (but the dark theme is ultimately resonant). Nor did I realize that this would be classified as "gay fiction." Before I realized all that I got about twenty pages into the book and was not sure it would be one that I could finish...too many characters that were initially confusing and not capturing my interest. But I persisted and got caught up in the train wreck of characters. No one is happy or good or compelling in a positive way. In the end, while I may get caught up in the story I just never enjoy books that doesn't have one solid, relatable character. Here, the characters are unhappily gay, latently gay, domestic abusers, suicidal or alcoholic. Unless all this unhappiness seduces you, I don't recommend this one, eventhough the VERY young writer may have potential as a storyteller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2761319691172688255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2315731025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315731025" />
    <a title="Cindy Wilkerson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57085836-cindy-wilkerson"><img alt="Cindy Wilkerson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594651364p2/57085836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315731025?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Wilkerson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Wilkerson" href="/user/show/57085836-cindy-wilkerson">Cindy Wilkerson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57085836-cindy-wilkerson?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57085836-cindy-wilkerson?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315731025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7832960213254266290"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Full disclosure, I’m still emotionally hungover from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22822858.A_Little_Life' title='A Little Life by Hanya Yanagihara' rel='nofollow noopener'> A Little Life</a>, so I’m not sure if my feelings are 100% accurate.<br/>Full of teen angst, unlikeable characters, New Orleans and murder, I found myself enjoying the bones of the story. My qualm being I wish the characters were developed a tad bit more, or at least their dynamic with one another (aka, I wish I could’ve seen more of them as kids).<br/>This was a quick read and I enjoyed the unveiling.</span>
  <span id="freeText7832960213254266290" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Full disclosure, I’m still emotionally hungover from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22822858.A_Little_Life" title="A Little Life by Hanya Yanagihara" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Little Life</a>, so I’m not sure if my feelings are 100% accurate.<br />Full of teen angst, unlikeable characters, New Orleans and murder, I found myself enjoying the bones of the story. My qualm being I wish the characters were developed a tad bit more, or at least their dynamic with one another (aka, I wish I could’ve seen more of them as kids).<br />This was a quick read and I enjoyed the unveiling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7832960213254266290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+4n+EsyBIk+RWQtsW83dtH5qXI3T637R74WYYSe5KS2RJdrR7oTQxf/nlJQys1sLlr6KnYuBKGEFXga34aBEHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m9NduV4bdTNt12RhVT+R2cClea0r13EqA6raqPsZs1Dxf3l6fB6HuQNp+5k8QRdmKHGvvXO9J5rpcUR+PQDeYg==')})
  }

were adored as angels, yet shunned as half-men.As we are drawn into their dark and luminous story, as the crowds of Venetians, Neopolitans, and Romans, noblemen and peasants, musicians, prelates, He spends his high school years sleeping with the girls-next-door while carrying on a scandalous affair with an older man. Romances with to-die-for Vegas Showgirls are balanced with late night liaisons with like-minded guys, until finally Joel falls in love and marries a talented and beautiful woman, starts a family, and has a pretty much picture perfect life. When an actor plays a character, he has to find out what makes them who they are; their needs, dreams, and fears. It’s a difficult thing to do, but sometimes the hardest role in an actor’s life is that of himself.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1556719.Christopher_Rice">About Christopher  Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1556719.Christopher_Rice"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1453358111p3/1556719.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4309459639267946191">Christopher Rice is the recipient of the Lambda Literary Award and is the New York Times bestselling author of A DENSITY OF SOULS and the Bram Stoker Award finalists THE HEAVENS RISE and THE VINES. He is the head writer and an executive producer of "The Vampire Chronicles", a television show based on the bestselling novels by his mother, Anne Rice. Together they penned RAMSES THE DAMNED: THE PASSI</span>
  <span id="freeText4309459639267946191" style="display:none">Christopher Rice is the recipient of the Lambda Literary Award and is the New York Times bestselling author of A DENSITY OF SOULS and the Bram Stoker Award finalists THE HEAVENS RISE and THE VINES. He is the head writer and an executive producer of "The Vampire Chronicles", a television show based on the bestselling novels by his mother, Anne Rice. Together they penned RAMSES THE DAMNED: THE PASSION OF CLEOPATRA, a sequel to her bestselling novel THE MUMMY OR RAMSES THE DAMNED. BONE MUSIC, the first installment in his new Burning Girl series, was released March 1st, 2018, and the sequel, BLOOD ECHO, now on sale. The third entry in the series, BLOOD VICTORY, is available for pre-order. With his best friend, New York Times bestselling novelist Eric Shaw Quinn, Christopher hosts the YouTube channel THE DINNER PARTY SHOW WITH CHRISTOPHER RICE &amp; ERIC SHAW QUINN (#TDPS). THE DINNER PARTY SHOW began as a podcast and Internet radio show. You can download and stream all of their episodes at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.TDPS.tv">www.TDPS.tv</a>. He lives in West Hollywood, California. Visit him at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.christopherricebooks.com">www.christopherricebooks.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4309459639267946191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
